          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Chrome is deprecating direct access to private network endpoints from public websites as part of the Private Network Access (PNA) specification (



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome is deprecating direct access to private network endpoints from public websites as part of the Private Network Access (PNA) specification (<!----></span>





https://developer.chrome.com/blog/private-network-access-preflight/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://developer.chrome.com/blog/private-network-access-preflight/"><!---->https://developer.chrome.com/blog/private-network-access-preflight/<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>





 Services listening on the localhost (127.0.0.0/8) are considered private according to the specification (



<span class="line"><!----> Services listening on the localhost (127.0.0.0/8) are considered private according to the specification (<!----></span>





https://wicg.github.io/private-network-access/#ip-address-space-heading



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://wicg.github.io/private-network-access/#ip-address-space-heading"><!---->https://wicg.github.io/private-network-access/#ip-address-space-heading<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>





 Chrome's PNA protection can be bypassed using the IP address 0.0.0.0 to access services listening on the localhost on macOS and Linux.



<span class="line"><!----> Chrome's PNA protection can be bypassed using the IP address 0.0.0.0 to access services listening on the localhost on macOS and Linux.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This can also be abused in DNS rebinding attacks targeting a web application listening on the localhost.



<span class="line"><!---->This can also be abused in DNS rebinding attacks targeting a web application listening on the localhost.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The impact is that an attacker can bypass Chrome's Private Network Access (PNA) protections to access HTTP resources listening on the localhost.



<span class="line"><!---->The impact is that an attacker can bypass Chrome's Private Network Access (PNA) protections to access HTTP resources listening on the localhost.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 98.0.4758.102 stable



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 98.0.4758.102 stable<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: macOS (12.2.1) & Linux (Ubuntu 21.10)



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: macOS (12.2.1) &amp; Linux (Ubuntu 21.10)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





The following test uses an HTML file hosted on a plaintext HTTP server. The victim needs to run a plaintext HTTP service listening on the localhost (127.0.0.1). For our test, the service on the localhost is hosting an image (favicon.ico in the example below). The sample HTML tries to access the image using an <img> HTML tag. The first <img> contains a src attribute pointing to the localhost. Chrome's PNS will block this access with the following console error: "Access to image at '



<span class="line"><!---->The following test uses an HTML file hosted on a plaintext HTTP server. The victim needs to run a plaintext HTTP service listening on the localhost (127.0.0.1). For our test, the service on the localhost is hosting an image (favicon.ico in the example below). The sample HTML tries to access the image using an &lt;img&gt; HTML tag. The first &lt;img&gt; contains a src attribute pointing to the localhost. Chrome's PNS will block this access with the following console error: "Access to image at '<!----></span>





http://localhost:8080/favicon.ico



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8080/favicon.ico"><!---->http://localhost:8080/favicon.ico<!----></a>





'



<span class="line"><!---->'<!----></span>





 from origin '



<span class="line"><!----> from origin '<!----></span>





http://example.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://example.com"><!---->http://example.com<!----></a>





'



<span class="line"><!---->'<!----></span>





 has been blocked by CORS policy: The request client is not a secure context and the resource is in more-private address space `local`." The second <img> contains a src attribute pointing to the 0.0.0.0 IP address. This image will be displayed in Chrome and bypasses the PNA protection.



<span class="line"><!----> has been blocked by CORS policy: The request client is not a secure context and the resource is in more-private address space `local`." The second &lt;img&gt; contains a src attribute pointing to the 0.0.0.0 IP address. This image will be displayed in Chrome and bypasses the PNA protection.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->The following HTML needs to be hosted on a plaintext HTTP server (accessed using <!----></span>





http://

):



<span class="line"><!---->):<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->&lt;!doctype html&gt;<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->&lt;html lang="en"&gt;<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->&lt;body&gt;<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->&lt;p&gt;Image localhost: &lt;img src="<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!----> alt="localhost test image"/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->&lt;p&gt;Image 0.0.0.0: &lt;img src="<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!----> alt="0.0.0.0 test image"/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<!----></span>

The ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED you see sounds like the poc.html does not have the correct image source URL as the browser can't connect.



<span class="line"><!---->The ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED you see sounds like the poc.html does not have the correct image source URL as the browser can't connect.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The attacker deploys poc.html on a HTTP server they control, e.g. a public server such as 



<span class="line"><!---->The attacker deploys poc.html on a HTTP server they control, e.g. a public server such as <!----></span>





http://www.example.com/poc.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://www.example.com/poc.html"><!---->http://www.example.com/poc.html<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 or on their LAN such as 



<span class="line"><!----> or on their LAN such as <!----></span>





http://www.example.local/poc.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://www.example.local/poc.html"><!---->http://www.example.local/poc.html<!----></a>





 - This can't be on the victim machine.



<span class="line"><!----> - This can't be on the victim machine.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The victim runs their own HTTP server on their own machine, listening on the localhost interface (e.g. 



<span class="line"><!---->The victim runs their own HTTP server on their own machine, listening on the localhost interface (e.g. <!----></span>





http://localhost:8000



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8000"><!---->http://localhost:8000<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>





 with an image or favicon deployed under root /.



<span class="line"><!----> with an image or favicon deployed under root /.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The poc.html file on attacker machine must include a link to the image served from the victim machine (e.g. 



<span class="line"><!---->The poc.html file on attacker machine must include a link to the image served from the victim machine (e.g. <!----></span>





http://localhost:8000/image.jpg



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8000/image.jpg"><!---->http://localhost:8000/image.jpg<!----></a>





 / 



<span class="line"><!----> / <!----></span>





http://0.0.0.0:8000/image.jpg



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://0.0.0.0:8000/image.jpg"><!---->http://0.0.0.0:8000/image.jpg<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->The victim browses to poc.html hosted on the attacker machine (e.g. <!----></span>





http://www.example.local/poc.html

)

 from their own machine. Chrome will load the second image (0.0.0.0) but not the first one (localhost).



<span class="line"><!----> from their own machine. Chrome will load the second image (0.0.0.0) but not the first one (localhost).<!----></span>

At least one DNS resolver that allows users to filter traffic using blocklists and another one that uses DoH, are both returning 0.0.0.0 for blocked hostnames instead of NXDOMAIN, thus DNS rebinding attacks on localhost are possible.



<span class="line"><!---->At least one DNS resolver that allows users to filter traffic using blocklists and another one that uses DoH, are both returning 0.0.0.0 for blocked hostnames instead of NXDOMAIN, thus DNS rebinding attacks on localhost are possible.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





People using those DNS resolvers might skew the above counter.



<span class="line"><!---->People using those DNS resolvers might skew the above counter.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To test, try as root:



<span class="line"><!---->To test, try as root:<!----></span>



<br>





# nc -l -p 443 -s 127.0.0.1



<span class="line"><!----># nc -l -p 443 -s 127.0.0.1<!----></span>



<br>





(or -s 0.0.0.0 or without those)



<span class="line"><!---->(or -s 0.0.0.0 or without those)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Then either make sure the DNS resolver returns 0.0.0.0 for



<span class="line"><!---->Then either make sure the DNS resolver returns 0.0.0.0 for<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://google.com"><!---->google.com<!----></a>





 and/or



<span class="line"><!----> and/or<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





accounts.google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://accounts.google.com"><!---->accounts.google.com<!----></a>





 and start chromium (which should attempt to open google by default)



<span class="line"><!----> and start chromium (which should attempt to open google by default)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But what you see instead is the netcat terminal receives some garbage text(a https attempt from chromium) which includes the hostname that it was tried ie.



<span class="line"><!---->But what you see instead is the netcat terminal receives some garbage text(a https attempt from chromium) which includes the hostname that it was tried ie.<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





accounts.google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://accounts.google.com"><!---->accounts.google.com<!----></a>



<br>





Or you can emulate the DNS resolver returning 0.0.0.0, by having this line in /etc/hosts:



<span class="line"><!---->Or you can emulate the DNS resolver returning 0.0.0.0, by having this line in /etc/hosts:<!----></span>



<br>





0.0.0.0



<span class="line"><!---->0.0.0.0<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





www.google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.google.com"><!---->www.google.com<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





accounts.google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://accounts.google.com"><!---->accounts.google.com<!----></a>



<br>





which functionally equivalent to the line:



<span class="line"><!---->which functionally equivalent to the line:<!----></span>



<br>





127.0.0.1



<span class="line"><!---->127.0.0.1<!----></span>

         * is disabled for this component.
